Seperating College Football Scores

2021-03-26

I am going to take CFB logs and seperate out the scores using code. Lets get started.

library(tidyverse)
## -- Attaching packages --------------------------------------- tidyverse 1.3.0 --
## v ggplot2 3.3.3     v purrr   0.3.4
## v tibble  3.0.5     v dplyr   1.0.3
## v tidyr   1.1.2     v stringr 1.4.0
## v readr   1.4.0     v forcats 0.5.0
## -- Conflicts ------------------------------------------ tidyverse_conflicts() --
## x dplyr::filter() masks stats::filter()
## x dplyr::lag()    masks stats::lag()
library(ggalt)
## Warning: package 'ggalt' was built under R version 4.0.4
## Registered S3 methods overwritten by 'ggalt':
##   method                  from   
##   grid.draw.absoluteGrob  ggplot2
##   grobHeight.absoluteGrob ggplot2
##   grobWidth.absoluteGrob  ggplot2

##   grobY.absoluteGrob      ggplot2

First, we corrall our data from a .csv file so we can get a hold of what we are actually trying to change.

logs <- read.csv("footballlogs20.csv")

By looking at the file, we notice that until the “Outcome” column, you get W/L followed by the score of the game inside parenthesis, like this: (x-y). Our first way to start splitting up the code is to seperate the W/L from the score.

logs %>% 
  separate(Result, into=c("Outcome", "Score"), sep=" ")

Great, we have successfully seperated the W/L from the score. Now, we can paste this same code again, but add another line to start removing the parenthesis.

logs %>% 
  separate(Result, into=c("Outcome", "Score"), sep=" ") %>% 
  separate(Score, into=c("TeamScore", "OpponentScore"), sep="\\(") %>% 
mutate(OpponentScore=gsub(")", "", OpponentScore)) %>%
  head()

Notice now that we still arent done. Our final step requires us to remove the “-” from between the figures, then slide the first score back into the “TeamScore” column.

splitlogs <- logs %>% 
  separate(Result, into=c("Outcome", "Score"), sep=" ") %>% 
  separate(Score, into=c("TeamScore", "OpponentScore"), sep="\\(") %>% 
mutate(OpponentScore=gsub(")", "", OpponentScore)) %>%
  separate(OpponentScore, into=c("TeamScore", "OpponentScore"), sep="-") %>%
  mutate(TeamScore = as.numeric(TeamScore), OpponentScore = as.numeric(OpponentScore))

Now, we set out to find the worst college football games of the year. We mutate a differential and then filter for only the games that were blowouts by more than 65 points.

worstgames <- splitlogs %>% mutate(Differential = TeamScore - OpponentScore) %>% filter(Differential > 65)

Lets see how that looks on a chart.

ggplot() + 
  geom_point(data=splitlogs, aes(x=TeamScore, y=OpponentScore), color="grey") + 
  geom_point(data=worstgames, aes(x=TeamScore, y=OpponentScore), color="red") + 
  geom_encircle(data=worstgames, aes(x=TeamScore, y=OpponentScore), s_shape=.00005, expand=.0000003, colour="red") +
  geom_text(aes(x=70, y=10, label="Worst Games")) + 
  labs(title="Seems like these bad games arent super common", subtitle="RIP to Georgia Tech", x="TeamScore", y="OpponentScore") + 
  theme_minimal() + 
  theme(
    plot.title = element_text(size = 16, face = "bold"),
    axis.title = element_text(size = 8), 
    plot.subtitle = element_text(size=10), 
    panel.grid.minor = element_blank()
    )
